<div id="review_718208042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718208042" />
    <a title="Shannon McDermott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23902198-shannon-mcdermott"><img alt="Shannon McDermott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520283813p2/23902198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718208042?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon McDermott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon McDermott" href="/user/show/23902198-shannon-mcdermott">Shannon McDermott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23902198-shannon-mcdermott?shelf=csff">csff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23902198-shannon-mcdermott?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23902198-shannon-mcdermott?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718208042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14193743667474208742">Eanrin has always known to never get involved in the affairs of mortals. If all Faeries had that policy, the Hidden Land would have lived out a happier story. But as the lost daughter of the Eldest walked a road darkened by Faerie, so her path will fatefully cross a Faerie’s again. And again.<br/><br/>In <i>Starflower</i>, Anne Elisabeth Stengl tells the story of Faeries who became involved with mortals, and mortals who became involved with Faeries. Not all were the better for it; nor were all the worst.<br/><br/><i>Starflow</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14193743667474208742" style="display:none">Eanrin has always known to never get involved in the affairs of mortals. If all Faeries had that policy, the Hidden Land would have lived out a happier story. But as the lost daughter of the Eldest walked a road darkened by Faerie, so her path will fatefully cross a Faerie’s again. And again.<br /><br />In <i>Starflower</i>, Anne Elisabeth Stengl tells the story of Faeries who became involved with mortals, and mortals who became involved with Faeries. Not all were the better for it; nor were all the worst.<br /><br /><i>Starflower</i> is sold as a fairy tale, and indeed it is. Pieces and elements from all sorts of fairy tales swirl in it – refined, changed, and woven together into a new whole. A few of the old tropes are played for humor – the lady in the tower, princes turned to frogs. Most are used more seriously – enchantments, fairies, shape-changing, dragons.<br /><br />One of Stengl’s most effective uses is of the law of Faerie. Everyone who has read fairy tales knows that Faerie has its laws, just as immutable as nature’s. In Faerie blessings are true, and curses are facts; vows must be kept, and names have power. Anne Elisabeth Stengl takes this strange code, builds it as surely into her world as the law of gravity, and lets the story flow in its courses.<br /><br />The Faerie characters are realized in the uniqueness of their nature and experience. But different as they are, they are not wholly alien, and readers can understand them like people. The humans in the story are just as finely done. Stengl handles her cast with great sympathy, making flawed characters likeable and villains pitiable.<br /><br />The world – or worlds, I could say – of <i>Starflower</i> beat with life. Some are grim, some are beautiful, some are treacherous, most are dangerous – but all are alive. You can almost feel the hot streets of Etalpalli, the humid swamp, the stony way to the Place of the Teeth.<br /><br />There is very little to criticize in this book. The most I can say is that I did not understand Starflower’s sudden distrust of the poet, nor did I consider it believable. In all its main elements, <i>Starflower</i> excelled. It is beautifully written, a pleasure to read. The spiritual strains in the story were profound and moving. The story was unexpected, and landscapes and people rose up brilliantly from the pages. This book was a surprise to me. I had expected it to be good, but I didn’t think it would be incredible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14193743667474208742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_451416335" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/451416335" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6901162-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526665403p2/6901162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/451416335?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/6901162-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6901162-meghan?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6901162-meghan?shelf=author-review-request">author-review-request</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6901162-meghan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451416335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15705732803353698817">Oh. My. Goodness. How have I not heard of this series yet?! How has it not crossed my path until now? This book was massively overflowing with wondrous magical beauty. I can say without a doubt that this book rivals any Faerie story that I have read to date, easily.<br/><br/>I did not head into this book with high expectations. But before long I was completely blown away. I am at awe at how beautifully this story is written, no, woven sounds like a much better word. Because it's more like a masterpiece th</span>
  <span id="freeText15705732803353698817" style="display:none">Oh. My. Goodness. How have I not heard of this series yet?! How has it not crossed my path until now? This book was massively overflowing with wondrous magical beauty. I can say without a doubt that this book rivals any Faerie story that I have read to date, easily.<br /><br />I did not head into this book with high expectations. But before long I was completely blown away. I am at awe at how beautifully this story is written, no, woven sounds like a much better word. Because it's more like a masterpiece than anything else. Can you tell that I loved it?! Seriously though, if you haven't read this book yet, or were completely unaware of this series existence, like myself. You need to get your hands on this right now. All fantasy fans everywhere, read this, pronto, immediately.<br /><br />This is book #4 in the series, but I read it without feeling like I was missing any details. I am thinking that the stories aren't completely related to each other. But I assure you I that I will be getting out there and reading the previous three installments as soon as I can. I have found a brand new author that I simply adore. Her writing carried me away into this amazing fantastical, and terrifying, stunning world. I was so sad when I closed the last pages because I was just not ready to go.<br /><br />The characters in the story were all so incredibly developed. I gushed to my husband repeatedly with quotes from the book, and the incredible descriptiveness, immensely vivid imagery, and the characters within that I just could not get enough of. It was also such a fun read because it was like watching this awesome puzzle come together. We were given all these pieces of information and events that were seemingly unrelated. But as the story came together and all the pieces connected, it made the story that much more epic. Anne really has created a story to be loved by all.<br /><br />I will be looking for more books by her, and definitely be wanting to read the rest of this series. Thank you so much to Anne for sending me her story. It's cast a spell on me and I've completely fallen in love. To all of you, I say again, go read this book. It's a must for any and all readers.</span>

<div id="review_480835787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/480835787" />
    <a title="Nikole Hahn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1794810-nikole-hahn"><img alt="Nikole Hahn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285131257p2/1794810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/480835787?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikole Hahn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikole Hahn" href="/user/show/1794810-nikole-hahn">Nikole Hahn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer480835787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12455535525367422696">Starflower by Anne Elisabeth Stengl is yet another novel from the Goldstone Wood Series filled with unique voices and humorous characters.<br/><br/>They say to create a great piece of writing you must read a variety of genres. Stengl inserts some Native American flavor into these stories as we hear about some of the characters from Veiled Rose and Moonblood like the boy who got lost on the Paths and Imeralda. We also learn more about Earin, the cat-man.<br/><br/>The story is less about Earin and more about Imeralda</span>
  <span id="freeText12455535525367422696" style="display:none">Starflower by Anne Elisabeth Stengl is yet another novel from the Goldstone Wood Series filled with unique voices and humorous characters.<br /><br />They say to create a great piece of writing you must read a variety of genres. Stengl inserts some Native American flavor into these stories as we hear about some of the characters from Veiled Rose and Moonblood like the boy who got lost on the Paths and Imeralda. We also learn more about Earin, the cat-man.<br /><br />The story is less about Earin and more about Imeralda–also known as Starflower. Starflower is from the Hidden Lands where women literally do not have a voice. They use sign language to speak to each other and men view them as property. Earin finds Starflower in an enchanted sleep next to a magical river.<br /><br />Earin is a cat and a man. He is a silly poet in love with Queen Bobos cousin, Gleamdren. Gleamdren is a shallow and vain girl who lets herself get kidnapped by Hri Sora, a dragon, who used to be Etalpali–a great queen whose hatred turned her into Dark Father’s daughter.<br /><br />The Dark Father strips her of her dragon form and her wings. Hri stands in human form bearing the power of her dragon’s fire in a frail human body. Hri is mother to the Black Dogs–her neglected children who know only hate until Starflower.<br /><br />The Black Dogs do Hri’s bidding and are known for dragging people to death’s dark waters. The lesson Stengl reveals between the Black Dogs and Starflower is how persistant love and courage can change someone who has only known hate and abuse.<br /><br />Starflower succeeds where Earin fails in bringing Gleamdren to safety, but only after Starflower makes a bargain. Starflower must face the past she ran from in order to free her people from the bondage of a deviate faerie lord once married to Hri. Hri wants Amarok dead. Starflower is not alone. Earin accompanies her and faces the danger with Starflower. Overall, Stengl’s novel, Starflower is just as good as the rest of her novels in the Goldstone Wood series and I rated it five stars. There is a good reason why Stengl won the Christy Award twice.<br /><br />*book given by publisher to review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12455535525367422696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_650471586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650471586" />
    <a title="Chelsea Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20791330-chelsea-johnson"><img alt="Chelsea Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575240028p2/20791330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650471586?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Johnson" href="/user/show/20791330-chelsea-johnson">Chelsea Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650471586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10369615461570418013">Yet another book that was difficult to put down. Anne Elisabeth Stengl's writing is amazing. She picks words that vividly paint a picture in the reader's mind. She's also managed to create a world that is deep, with it's own set of histories/legends. Almost as if it's been around for years in more than just pen and paper. <br/><br/>Set around 1600 years before the events that unfolded beginning in <i>Heartless</i> and moving on through <i>Veiled Rose</i> and <i>Moonblood</i>, <i>Starflower</i> allows us to see the back story behind </span>
  <span id="freeText10369615461570418013" style="display:none">Yet another book that was difficult to put down. Anne Elisabeth Stengl's writing is amazing. She picks words that vividly paint a picture in the reader's mind. She's also managed to create a world that is deep, with it's own set of histories/legends. Almost as if it's been around for years in more than just pen and paper. <br /><br />Set around 1600 years before the events that unfolded beginning in <i>Heartless</i> and moving on through <i>Veiled Rose</i> and <i>Moonblood</i>, <i>Starflower</i> allows us to see the back story behind some characters:<br /><br />Eanrin: The bard, Chief Poet of Rudiobus, both man and cat, very much in love with Lady Gleamdren (or is he?)<br /><br />Starflower: Mortal maid, cursed, silenced but with a voice that's stronger than most<br /><br />Hri Sora: (aka The Dragonwitch), angry, out for revenge<br /><br />Glomar: Captain of Iubdan's guards, both badger and man, very much in love with Lady Gleamdren<br /><br />Gleamdren: Cousin of Queen Bebo, one of the keepers of the Secret of the Flowing Gold, kind of spoiled, object of every man's affection (at least she wishes)<br /><br />From the beginning, where we first met Eanrin he somehow managed to endear himself to me despite being really quite conceited and self-absorbed. I grew to like him even more once he found Imraldera and started to fully understand what it meant to truly love. Of course Starflower, was the complete opposite of Eanrin from the start and you couldn't help but feel bad for her--she'd been cursed with no voice from the moment she was born, that being said, even though women were seen as not much more than slaves, she managed to hold onto her fire and was made strong through the love from her mother and then the love she showed her sister. She even managed to find the strength to stand up to the Beast and see to his destruction so that her sister could be free of the curse even if it meant probably never seeing her again.<br /><br />I highly recommend the entire<i>Tales of Goldstone Wood</i> series to anyone, especially those who love fantasy and fairy tales. I do suggest going in order for the most part since the books tend to kind of build on one another as well as go deeper into things that were only mentioned previously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10369615461570418013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_422634872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422634872" />
    <a title="Rachelle Sperling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10712883-rachelle-sperling"><img alt="Rachelle Sperling" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422634872?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachelle Sperling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachelle Sperling" href="/user/show/10712883-rachelle-sperling">Rachelle Sperling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422634872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17634795944359067000">Before I speak of Starflower I must speak of the Tales of the Goldstone Wood series as a whole. Book one is Heartless. Book two is Veiled Rose. Book three is Moonblood and the fourth book is Starflower. Each book stands alone, however, they work together so beautifully as a series I highly recommend that you read them together.<br/><br/>In a recent blog I referred to the power of story (the power of myth), and how it helps us see our own stories. The Tales of the Goldstone Wood gave that gift to me. They </span>
  <span id="freeText17634795944359067000" style="display:none">Before I speak of Starflower I must speak of the Tales of the Goldstone Wood series as a whole. Book one is Heartless. Book two is Veiled Rose. Book three is Moonblood and the fourth book is Starflower. Each book stands alone, however, they work together so beautifully as a series I highly recommend that you read them together.<br /><br />In a recent blog I referred to the power of story (the power of myth), and how it helps us see our own stories. The Tales of the Goldstone Wood gave that gift to me. They are more than slightly, but not completely allegorical, after the manner of Narnia. However their real comparison, in my mind, would be C.S. Lewis' Till We Have Faces: A Myth Retold.<br /><br />I've already read several of these books more than once and each time I find more depth. They hold so much truth to be uncovered. They are together the story of the Beloved.<br /><br />Beloved bride. Beloved children. Beloved lost. Beloved.<br /><br />They are stories of death and resurrection. Rebellion and redemption. Friendship and Betrayal. The books visit lands of myth and mystery and in that world they give us a glimpse of the greatest story of all: the story of our Father, our Bridegroom, our Guide seeking His Beloved.<br /><br />Not only do these stories illustrate fabulous truth, they are delightfully told. I COULD NOT PUT THEM DOWN. I can't even begin to describe the creativity of these tales. Take for example the myth of the unicorn. In Heartless we are introduced to the songs of unicorn fry. (I pictured them as seahorses.) Then in Moonblood we meet the Unicorn and discover the song that he once sang. He is both brilliant and hideous: endowed with glory and undeniably fallen - a mastery of storytelling.<br /><br />Each character, be it person or fairy or river or wood is fabulously developed and each story weaves through the others like a beautiful symphony.<br /><br />Starflower, in particular, is the story of knowing and being known by your true name. I give it my highest star rating - 5 stars off the chart.<br /><br />I received a free digital copy of this book in exchange for my honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17634795944359067000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('orkFdbI1Z4iFBjHpb+MrQNnz9fW7KWsOwqbgEsVYHWiYNq4nCYXur+lH2q45y5gSjgyz6qUNbjtIbOWS2Qjk/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RAvMaLolnkRPd10ZOAJe+PvchKNKPCzPfn302aQ6rKJ+hGc6AZUXYyM2tl5uKu2qrCPCvFQYKfr0t/FZuGpVNQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6644795612586419961">Anne Elisabeth Stengl makes her home in Raleigh, North Carolina, where she lives with her husband, Rohan, a passel of cats, and one long-suffering dog. When she's not writing, she enjoys Shakespeare, opera, and tea, and studies piano, painting, and pastry baking. She studied illustration at Grace College and English literature at Campbell University. She is the author of the TALES OF GOLDSTONE WOO</span>
  <span id="freeText6644795612586419961" style="display:none">Anne Elisabeth Stengl makes her home in Raleigh, North Carolina, where she lives with her husband, Rohan, a passel of cats, and one long-suffering dog. When she's not writing, she enjoys Shakespeare, opera, and tea, and studies piano, painting, and pastry baking. She studied illustration at Grace College and English literature at Campbell University. She is the author of the TALES OF GOLDSTONE WOOD, which currently includes seven novels and two novellas, with plenty more works due to release over the next few years. Her novels HEARTLESS, VEILED ROSE, and DRAGONWITCH have each been honored with a Christy Award, and STARFLOWER was voted winner of the 2013 Clive Staples Award.</span>
